Summary
Caster of Magic Warlord mod's main goal is to improve immersion and reduce repetition when using normal
military units. Normal units have been redesigned, and several dozen new stock and racial unique units (with
complete new animated sprites) have been added across the board.
The units recruited from Armorer's Guild and Fantastic Stable buildings typically cost more and are far more
advanced than their Caster of Magic counterparts. These units are not part of the Caster of Magic design of
being disposable and inferior to summons and spammed all over the world to the point of clutter.
Four new races have also been introduced – Xuanyuan, Hawkmen, Rakhshasa, and Goblin
The mod also considers asymmetric game balance to be a key factor to game enjoyment to stay true to the spirit
of Master of Magic. There will be moments where you might wonder an individual element is unusually strong –
for the most part that is intentional though minor balancing tweaks will continue with future versions.
There have been spell modifications, including entirely new summon units. Two additional uncommon (total 12)
and three rare tier spells (total 18) are available for research. Realms have been re-balanced accordingly and
magic realm themes have been preserved.
Gold and food maintenance of units have been adjusted to lessen unit spam, particularly for AI wizards.
Economic buildings with lower upkeep to prevent them being a drain to your coffers (only your military and rush-
buying should be).
Races, heroes, and building mechanics have also been redesigned to fit the modder vision, then heavily play-
tested with balance taken into consideration. Some of these updates reverse changes from Caster of Magic to
something closer to the original Master of Magic, albeit not completely. There are also visual changes.
Additional changes across the board are for you to discover. Many are not included in this manual as they are
not related to gameplay, just immersion.
Installation
How to install (1.5.12.5):
1) Uninstall/unload old version of mod (see below) ****
2) Create folder “Master of Magic Caster Windows 1.5.11”.
3) Copy all content inside folder “Master of Magic Caster Windows” to “Master of Magic Caster Windows
1.5.11”
4) Install patch of Caster of Magic for windows version 1.5.11 (which could be found here:
https://www.realmsbeyond.net/forums/showthread.php?tid=11090) by copy content from folder
“CoMWin1511” inside the zip file into folder “Master of Magic Caster Windows 1.5.11”.
5) Unpack "CoM2ModWarlord1.5.12.5.7z" into "...\Master of Magic Caster Windows 1.5.11\Mods" folder.
6) Run caster of magic for windows 1.5.11 from folder “Master of Magic Caster Windows 1.5.11” until reach
main menu.
7) Choose the "Load Mod" option in the lower right corner.
8) Type mod name "WARLORD" and enter. This will automatically load mod files into the data folder while
original file in data folder would be backup for sake of later reversion. (In case you have your own
customize artifact, backup your own "items.dat" before doing so or you would lose them.)
9) Once the process is completed, game will automatically exit.
10) Run caster of magic for windows again, now game would become Caster of Magic for Windows:
Warlord.
11) Please play the game with these setting…
- Pick “Use Legacy Tileset” (to activate Civizard tileset)
- Pick “Remove Tree” (so that tree in combat would not be too messy)
How to reset environments setting back to original (tile back to legacy tileset, raise volcano animation,
combat vegetation and combat item as well as music back to original)
1) Copy content in folder “mods\Warlord\backup original environment\” to “data” folder.
2) Now you are free to pick “Remove Tree” or not pick “Use Legacy Tileset” setting.
How to reset music back to original only.
1) Copy content in folder “mods\Warlord\backup original environment\music” to “data\music” folder.
How to uninstall the mod.
1) Go to the main menu.
2) Click "Unload Mod" option on lower right corner. Game will automatically unload the mod and replacing
them with backup files (not included your own items in "items.dat", this one must be done by yourself)
3) Game would exit upon completing process.
4) Restart the game and game would be back to become original Caster of Magic for Windows without
Warlord mod.
Book System and Retorts has been modified:
• How many spells are granted per book. The new system is fully symmetrical (1-3-4-5-6-7-8-10)
• being able to research a single common-tier spell at random for all realms without books chosen.
• Starting Power Changed. Every book always grants starting power and skill, not just when you have 4+
books of a type. Book 3 to Book 4 no longer grants +6 starting power.
• Starting Power Formula is now 9 + 1 for books 1-7 + 2 for books 8-9 + 3 for books 10-11 and +4 for book
12
• Starting skill follows fairly closely, though due to different method of calculation may be slightly lower for
first 3 books of a type.
• Guaranteed very rares eliminated
• Guaranteed rares limited to book 10 only (as guaranteed early rare)
• Book-based discounts changed from 8% research / 5% spell per book starting book #9 to 5% research
(starting book #6) and 3% (starting book #7)
• Books 9 and 10 grant an additional starting common spell.
The amount of starting overland skill is approximately 2 to 4 below Caster of Magic (reduction of 1 per 3 books)
to balance city vs magic production early in the game (given the changes that took place in city mechanics)

Retorts
Retorts have been reworked with some retorts change, all of them get spells exclusive to their own.
Alchemy Alchemist:
The wizard is an expert in the art of Alchemy.
• Allows the wizard to convert gold to mana and mana to gold at a rate of 1:1.
• All non-summoned units trained by the wizard from non-Barbarian cities gain magic weapons.
• Alchemist's Guild cost 15% cheaper.
• Could access to spell “Philosopher’s Stone”.
• Costs 2 picks.
Warlord:
The wizard is a renowned militarist.
• All non-summoned units under the wizard's control have their veterancy level increased by one.
• Allows non-summoned units to exceed their normal veterancy limit by one level.
• Barracks, War College, Armory, Fighter's Guild, Armorer's Guild, City Wall, Fortification, Hillfort, and
Warlord's Hold cost 15% cheaper.
• Warlord could utilize global ability of Warlord's Hold regardless of home race.
• Could access to spell “Wall of Stone”.
• Could access to spell “Mark of Conqueror”.
• Mutually exclusive with the Tactician retort at the start of the game.
• Costs 2 picks.
Channeler:
The wizard has mastered the art of channeling spellcraft.
• Allows the wizard to cast spells without range penalties.
• Reduces spell range penalties during banishment by half.
• Reduces overall spell upkeep by 50%.
• Reduces the cost of casting spells in combat by 12%.
• Could access to spell “Marionette”.
• Could access to reform “Marionette Ascension”.
• Costs 2 picks.
Archmage:
The wizard is a renowned master in teaching and training spell casting.
• Increases both already acquired and newly produced skill points (SP) by 50%.
• Could access to reform “Archmage’s Tutition”.
• Could access to reform “Archmage’s Mentorship”.
Artificer:
The wizard is a master craftsman who is an expert in magical engineering.
• Reduces the cost of making items/artifacts by 50%.
• Starts the game with the "Enchant Item" spell already researched.
• The "Create Artifact" spell will be the first researchable Rare level spell.
• All mechanical units trained by the wizard gain +1 Melee/Range Attack, +1 Armor, +1 Resistance, +1
Movement Point, and magic weapons.
• Could access to spell “Clockwork Tinmen”.
• Could access to spell “Clockwork Factory”.
• Could access to spell “Rebuild”.
Conjurer:
The wizard is an expert in conjuring magical creatures.
• Reduces the casting costs of all summoning spells by 25%.
• Reduces the research costs of all summoning spells by 25%.
• Reduces the total upkeep cost of Fantastic creatures by 25%.
• Starts the game with the "Summoning Circle" spell already researched.
• Could access to spell “Conjuring Pact”.
• Could access to spell “Spirit Link”.
Sage Master:
The wizard is a renowned scholar.
• Increases total research points generated each turn by 33%.
• Increases research points by 15 RP each turn.
• Library, University, Sage's Guild, Academy, and Ludus Agoge cost 15% cheaper.
• Could access to reform “Education Reform”.
• Could access to spell “Arcane Conference”.
Myrran:
The wizard is native to the plane of Myrror.
• Starts the game with a fortress on the plane of Myrror.
• Allows the player to choose Myrran races as their home race.
• Adjusts the starting positions of AI wizards accordingly.
• Could access to spell “Astral Gate”.
Guardian:
The wizard is respected as the guardian protector of his people.
• Increases the maximum population of the home race's city by 6 units.
• In combat, all units controlled by the wizard gain +10% To-Hit, +10% To-Defend, and +1 Resistance
when defending the city controlled by the wizard.
• Could access to reform “Lord Liberator”.
• Could access to reform “Lord Protector”.
• Costs 2 picks.
Famous Benefactor:
The wizard is well-known as a benefactor who willingly lends a hand to those who serve under them.
• Starts the game with 30 fame, and the "Heroic Heart" spell already researched.
• All heroes controlled by the wizard gain +2 Melee/Range Attack, +1 Armor, and +1 Resistance.
• 2x chance for artifact merchants, and 4x chance for mercenaries offer.
• If have enough gold, a hero is guaranteed to appear for hire in January, an item merchant appears in
July and mercenaries always show up in April and October starting in 1502.
• Heroes and mercenaries offering to join will be at a 1 level higher than usual and hiring cost of them do
not increase by their level.
• Could access to spell “Bountiful Festivity”.
Runemaster:
The wizard has mastered the power of rune language.
• Reduces research costs of Arcane spells by 50%.
• Reduces casting costs of overland spells (except Arcane, summons, and enchantments) by 25%.
• Reduces casting costs of overland Arcane spells (except item creation, and summons) by 50%.
• Reduces casting costs of combat Arcane spells by 25%.
• The effects of dispel-type spells cast by the wizard are 100% more effective.
• Starts the game with the "Dispel Magic" spell already researched.
• Could access to spell “Rune Formation Array”.
Charismatic:
The wizard possesses an unnatural presence that dramatically improves his dealings with others.
• Reduces the costs for hiring heroes, mercenaries, and purchasing magical items by half.
• Reduces the unrest level in all cities owned by the wizard by 1.
• Halves all diplomatic penalties from negative actions.
• Doubles all positive diplomatic effects.
• Offers made by the wizard are significantly more likely to be accepted.
• Could access to spell “Rally”.
• Could access to spell “Denoucement”.
• Could access to spell “Persuasive Whisperer”.
Specialist:
The wizard invests their skill and effort into mastering their primary realm. Primary realm is determined
by the realm with the highest number of books. In case of a tie, specialist realms are prioritized in this order:
Nature, Sorcery, Chaos, Life, and Death.
• Reduces the casting costs for spells in the wizard's primary realm by 12%.
• Reduces the research costs for spells in the wizard's primary realm by 12%.
• Increases dispel resistance for spells in the wizard's primary realm by 50%.
• Could access to reform “Gaia Mastery”.
• Could access to reform “AEther Mastery”.
• Could access to reform “Chaos Mastery”.
• Could access to reform “Life Mastery”.
• Could access to reform “Death Mastery”.
Tactician:
The wizard is renowned for their skill in maneuvering troops in combat.
• The wizard can sneak attack, making defenders lose their first action unless it's another wizard's
fortress, they have Tactician, or Supernatural Primal power protects them.
• All the wizard's units gain +1 Armor.
• The wizard's teleporting units gain First Strike.
• The wizard's Non-Corporeal units gain Negate First Strike.
• The wizard's units with a terrain bonus gain double the bonus, First Strike, and Negate First Strike.
• Gets a bonus in strategic combat.
• Could access to spell “Tactical Drill”.
• Could access to spell “Tactical Recall”.
• Could access to spell “Strategic Recall”.
• Costs 2 picks.
• Mutually exclusive with the Warlord retort at the start of the game.
Omniscient Procurator:
The wizard is an expert in managerial and statecraft.
• Reduces "Indirect Control" and "Banished" city penalties by 25%.
• Triples the "Administrative Skill" bonus.
• Could access to spell “Town Portal”.
Cult Leader:
The Wizard is the leader of a religion/cult with strong influence over the believers. Religious buildings
include the Shrine, Monastery, Witches' Convent, Cathedral, and Temple. Certain buildings and city
enchantments may be sanctified into religious buildings through certain spells.
• Increases the power generated by religious buildings by 100%.
• Increases the unrest reduction by religious buildings by 50% (rounded down).
• Could access to spell “Gospel of Evangelism”.
• Could access to spell “Divine Judgement”.
Astrologer:
The wizard is an expert in predicting and manipulating destiny by reading stars.
• Nodes controlled by the wizard produce +2 power for each year passed since the start of the game.
• Immune to spell-countering effects from nodes.
• Could access to spell “Dishearten Prophesy”.
• Could access to spell “Lucky Star”.
• Costs 2 picks.
Spellweaver Enchanter:
The wizard is an expert in the art of enchantment.
• Reduces the cost of enchantment/curse spells cast by the wizard by 25%.
• Increases dispel resistance of all enchantments/curses cast by the wizard by 150%.
• Could access to reform “Tatto Magic”.
• Could access to spell “Domain of Enchanter”.
• Costs 2 picks.
Difficulties
Game difficulty settings in Warlord mod have been adjusted relative to Caster of Magic, with the following key
points:
• AI upkeep multiplier is for the most part removed. AI doesn't need upkeep immunity to stay challenging.
This reduces unit spam considerably.
• AI overland spell casting cost multiplier is toned down.
• Easiest 2 difficulties do not penalize AI resources. Instead, player is rewarded with power and
production bonuses
• Hardest difficulties do not reward AI resources as much. Instead, player is handicapped with various city
economy penalties.
• The 'stalling' AI tactic is introduced in 'advanced' difficulty, tailored towards challenge-seeking playersBeginner Easy Normal Fair Advanced Expert Master Lunatic Phantasm

Building and City Changes:
Summary: Early city progression is slowed due to generally higher production costs, reduction in early fixed
production bonuses, and less accessible higher-tier production buildings. The changes partially bring back the
city progression pace of the original Master of Magic early game through late game. The amount of starting
overland skill is approximately 2 to 4 below Caster of Magic to balance city vs magic production early in the
game.
Economy buildings are more interconnected via pre-requisites (dependencies) and are inspired by a few building
tree mechanics choices from the original Master of Magic. Tree of knowledge carries a higher research and
casting cost (2000 and 250, respectively) and also unlocks Maritime's Guild, Wizard's Guild and Amplifying
Tower. Unlocked economy buildings all share the same building prerequisite: Sage's Guild.
Several economy buildings take more time to build, but gold maintenance of economy buildings generally
reduced with a city with all buildings typically saving roughly 20 gold per turn. However, there are 2 contributors
to gold loss in this mod: non-capital income penalty, and higher unit upkeep costs. What makes you poor is not
your own cities simply existing, but having an excessive number of units. This helps make game less cluttered
and come with end turn savings.
Early military aided by bringing back Master of Magic's Armory as an early recruitment building. It requires more
investment to develop a military city that pumps out experienced and magic-weapon units. This was needed to
balance the superior, less disposable nature of normal units.
Non-Capital cities are less productive, they receive a penalty to gold, food, production, power based on their
distance from capital city.
Mountain terrain have a 5% production bonus (instead of 7%). Volcanic terrain retain their 7% bonus.
Trade income cap per city is now 2% per pop (from 3% per pop).
Early Buildings:
Mill (cost 80/1) – No longer a massive production boost to new towns. Redesigned to grant 1 prod + ½
production per active farmer, yielding significantly more hammers in large cities (v 1.4.17 adjusted rounding
issues). Sawmill is no longer an essential early building to jump start a new town's production.
Dock (cost 120/0) – Now grants 1 food per ocean, coast, and rivermouth tile
NEW! Shipyard (cost 300/1) – Split from Dock and become requirement for Galley and Fire Galley
Smithy (cost 75/0) – Grants 3 fixed production (4+ in good terrain) and most units no longer require it.
Alchemist's Guild (cost 150/2) Alchemist Guild now grants +2 research – bringing back the original master of
magic feature of it granting a minor economy bonus. Cost is noticeably higher however.
Barracks (cost 200/1) – Barracks, which now require armory, delays starting experience boosts similar to
Original Master of Magic. This is needed to balance the enhanced stats among starter units and helps keep
them viable for a bit longer due to their low recruitment cost, while benefiting later units as well.
NEW! Armory (cost 150/1) – Armory has been restored from original Master of Magic, being the building for
recruiting the next tier of spearmen units (e.g. halberdiers), a few unique racial units below the level of Fighter's
Guild, and a secondary requirement for many support units like magisters. Units from armory typically a midpoint
between starter units and fighter's guild units. They tend to be cost effective and melee-oriented.
Fighter's Guild (cost 200/2) – Recruits the next tier of swordsmen, bowmen, and cavalry units (all unique to
Warlord mod) if permitted by race, as well as a few unique racial units. Troops more advanced than what is
provided by Armory.
War College (cost 540/3), now requires Fighter's Guilds and grants a racial unique unit for two races (Dwarf,
Gnoll), both cost effective given they recruit with a minimum of veteran experience level. War College help keep
bottom-tier and mid-tier units viable due to their lower recruitment cost while waiting for Tree of Knowledge.
Stables (cost 120/2) – Grants 4 fixed production (5 to 6 in good terrain).
Miner's Guild (cost 200/2) - Considerably more expensive, worth building once town is reasonably grown.
Mechanician's Guild (cost 400/4) – Changed to give +1.5 prod per worker (w/ +1/2 from town hall it adds to +2).
Considerably more expensive, worth building once town is reasonably grown. This building increasing
opportunity cost when accomodating food upkeep.
Also grants 2 mid-tier mechanical units of higher usefulness than Caster of Magic's catapult.
Town Hall (cost 80/0) – (previously known as Builder Hall) Allows buildings associated with advanced
civilizations, but also grants 0.5 production per worker, which is approximately a 15-20% production boost.
Marketplace (80/0). Income reduced to 7 (from 8).
Farmer's Market (cost 150/1) – Population growth bonus reduced by 10. Instead of granting food, Farmer's
Market grants 0.5 gold per population.
NEW! Brewery (cost 200/2) – Consume portion of Foods produce in city based on number of pop unit and
convert to gold at rate 4 Gold per Food.
Forester's Guild (130/1). Grants 4 food but gives +2 for each wild game resource in vicinity.
Magic Market (100/0) – had power income reduced to 4.
Library (80/0) – had research income reduced to 4.
Monument (75/0).
University (180/1).
Monastery (aka. Parthenon) (cost 200/1) – Priests no longer recruited here.
Cathedral (cost 500/2) Cathedral allows inquisitors (high men) and now grants 2 unrest reduction.
NEW! Temple (cost 400/1) – the alternative of Cathedral for some races, allows priests. The alternative Temple
building only grants 4 power and 1 unrest, but can be built faster and grants 3 power and 1 unrest for each
nightshade, orihalcon ,and wild game tile in the vicinity of town.
NEW! Witches’ Convent (cost 400/3) – Generates 4 religious power and curses enemy units when the city is
attacked.
NEW! Fortification (cost 600/5) – Requires mechanician guild and wall – All units inside city walls gain 'large
shield' effect and city in combat is surrounded by ocean tiles, thus impassable unless water walking, non-
corporeal, or flying. If playing with automatic combat, it grants +4 defense to units.
NEW! Hillfort (cost 300/3) – Only available for a few races, surround city with impassable cliff face with some
choke point to move through. Units inside city area also get Missile Immunity.
NEW! Warlord’s Hold (cost 400/5) – Only available for raider races, double strength of unrest reduction through
garrison and reduces cost of unit recruitment by 25%.
Oracle (cost 360/2)
Advanced Buildings:
Sage's Guild (400/2). Requires University. Grants access to most advanced economy buildings: Linking
Towers, Amplifying Tower, Wizard's Guild. All 3 are now linked to 'Tree of Knowledge'
Amplifying Tower (900/7) Wizard's Guild (800/3) Linking Towers (500/4) all require Sage's Guild and Tree of
Knowledge and intended to be part of late game. You will no longer see high caster units dominating the early
game.
• Note: Wizard's Guild now grants 12 power and 2 research.
Maritime Guild (cost 450/3) and requires Tree of Knowledge. However, warships are far superior in this mod.
Armorer's Guild (cost 600/4) and Fantastic Stables (cost 750/4) with a significantly less accessible 'Tree of
Knowledge' delays their usage by a couple of years relative to unmodded Caster of Magic.
NEW! Hangar (cost 400/3) is a requirement for flying mechanical units.
The units recruited from these buildings typically cost 240-300, require 2 Food, and are far more advanced than
their Caster of Magic counterparts. These units are not part of the Caster of Magic design of being disposable
and inferior to summons and spammed all over the world to the point of clutter. These units, many of which
benefit immensely from buffs, can compete against uncommon and rare tier summons and in groups assisted by
spells be capable of defeating top tier summons.
Building Tree:
Ships: Sawmill → (Shipyard + Fighter's) → Maritime
Wood Production: Sawmill → Forester's Guild
Production: (Miner's Guild + University) → (Mechanician's Guild + Wall) → Fortification
Food: (Granary + marketplace) → Farmer's Market
(Granary + Forester's) → Animist Guild
Research: Library + Builder's Hall → (University + Alchemist Guild) → Sage's Guild
Magic: Marketplace → Magic Market + Sage's Guild → Wizard's Guild
Combat Skill: (Monument + Sage's Guild) → Linking Tower
Overland skill: Sage's Guild → Amplifying Tower
Gold: (Marketplace + University) → (Bank + shipyard) → Merchant's Guild
Military: Armory → Fighter's Guild → Coliseum/War College/Armorer's Guild/Fantastic Stables
Armory → Barracks → War College (with Fighter's Guild)
Fighter's Guild + Barracks grant Colosseum, also grants War College (with Fighter's Guild)
Religion: (Shrine + Town Hall)→ Oracle and Monastery. Monastery → Cathedral/Temple
(Shrine + Magic Market) → Witches’ Convent.
Note that Tree of Knowledge unlocks Amplifying Tower, Linking towers, Wizard's Guild, Armorer's Guild,
Fantastic Stable, and Maritime Guild

Spearmen used mainly for unrest reduction at a minimum cost, but the high figure count allows buff strategies
against non-ranged units and cheap early game stacks. The original spearmen's role was too limited to be of
use, filling a mostly useless slot (given that swordsmen are more durable for sacrificial units when engaging in
wars of attrition via spells). Delayed access to barracks keep these from getting too useful.
Swordsmen (smithy), Bowmen (sawill + smithy), and Cavalry (stables + smithy) are the stock low-tier units.
Swordsmen have decent melee, high armor vs ranged and spells, and perform well if aided by experience
boosters and unit enchantments. Bowmen are your traditional ranged units, the extra 5% to hit helps them be
more accurate at mid-range. Cavalry (unchanged from caster of magic) are your fast, tactical unit, but highly
vulnerable to multi-figure attacks. Delayed access to barracks keep these enhanced bottom-tier units balanced.
Halberdiers (armory) are superior to swordsmen, particularly when facing other melee units. They are designed
to be more like their Master of Magic armory units in terms of cost and effectiveness, thus they lose 1 resistance,
1 racial special attack, and 10 cost.
Crossbowmen (fighter's guild + library) are the next bowmen tier, have fewer figures, but attack with armor
piercing shots and protect themselves with large shield. They are however vulnerable to melee.
Shieldbearers (fighter's guild) are the next swordsmen tier. These have mediocre melee damage output for the
cost (same as halberdier), but come with higher movement and very high armor, particularly against ranged and
magical attacks thanks to their large shield perk.
Heavy Cavalry (fighter's guild + stables) are the next cavalry tier, with higher stats across the board but 1 less
movement. First strike can be highly effective with 7 base attack, and the armor deficiency of Cavalry is lessened
with 4 base armor rating, making this a well-rounded tactical unit.
Shamans (shrine) and Monks (monastery) only differ by their movement rating. Priests (cathedral) now carry 2
healing charges and 1 resist to all making them a very impactful support unit, but have poor damage potential,
high upkeep cost, and require Temple, a pretty advanced building. These units do not count as trespassers
when you have a wizard's pact.
Disciples (sage's guild) are low-tier mages. Magisters (wizard's guild + armory) are mages that have large
shield instead of missile immunity, to simulate magic resistance. Along with 2 extra shots, this is generally an
improvement, thus are balanced out by having 1 fewer movement point.
Mechanician's Guild is much harder to build, thus stock units from it are superior. Catapults are now more
damaging, durable, and carry more ammo. Ballista is an alternative mechanical unit that loses wall crushing,
vulnerable to missile immunity in favor of armor piercing shots. These units give economy-oriented races viable
defenses
Triremes (dock) and Galleys (shipyard + armory) are unchanged but gold upkeeps are returning to ships Fire
Galley (shipyard + mechanician guild) are a more melee-oriented, faster ship that can attack flyers. Warships
come with higher stats and a much higher cost and upkeep with fewer races being able to build these and tree of
knowledge now needed to unlock Maritime's Guild.
Engineers (university + town hall) can now move, cast 'sapping wall' and buff mechanical units by +20% To-Hit
and +10% To-Defend, giving them tactical use in battle. Their cost and building requirements have been
increased due to them building roads 50% faster than unmodded engineers.
Pioneers (town hall + fighter's guild) are inferior engineers for some races that do not specialize on road
building, build 33% as fast as a modded engineer (and 50% as fast as unmodded engineers). These may be
subject to change as effect on elves and halflings are being reviewed.
Armorer Guild and Fantastic Stable unit – typically cost 240-300 5-6 gold upkeep 2 food upkeep.
These top-tier units are not part of the Caster of Magic design of being disposable and inferior to summons.
These units, many of which benefit immensely from buffs, can compete against uncommon and rare tier
summons and in groups assisted by spells be capable of defeating top tier summons.

It's important to note that your leader's race now depends on your choice at the
beginning of the game and is not affected by the location of your fortress
Race Summary / Units:
Intro: Brief race descriptions and general strategies have been included in the manual to ease the player into
trying out each race. Unit stats were kept hidden in the manual for conciseness and also to preserve the
excitement of discovery when noticing new units.
Note that some normal units will come with spell charges, some of which cannot be countered.
Barbarian:
Military-Oriented Gameplay
Characteristics: 90 growth, +30 outpost growth, Cheap settlers,
Special Building: Altar of Storm (required shore)
Building Limitations: Alchemist's Guild, (+Sage's Guild, +Wizard's Guild, +Amplifying Tower, +Linking Towers),
Monastery, (+Cathedral/Temple), Bank, (+Merchant's Guild), Armorer's Guild, Fantastic Stables, Mechanician's
Guild (+Fortification, +Hanger)
Barbarian design is to overwhelm opponents early on with mobile overland units (pathfinding) that deal very
high-damage due to having an innate +10% to hit and extra thrown secondary attacks. The high outpost and city
growth and cheap settlers ensure you have numerous sufficiently developed military centers producing strong
mid-tier units (Barbarians lack a top tier unit). If military superiority on land is not enough, barbarians also rule
the seas via a unique naval ship.
Note: barbarians no longer have a resistance penalty.
They have access to the majority of unrest-reduction and production buildings to ensure population remains
loyal and productive to your cause. However, Barbarians have severe limitations to strictly gold and power
sources, thus players must engage in conquest to stay competitive. The current design addresses some of the
issues that made race inferior in Master of Magic. However, a different balancing method was applied to restore
the race's themes and challenges the notion that a race must have access to several advanced buildings, even
wizard's guild, to stay competitive.
Normal Units: +10% To-Hit, Pathfinder, +Thrown (up to 4 per figure)
Spearmen, Swordsmen, Bowmen, Cavalry, Shamans, Heavy Cavalry.
Generic Mechanical Units: +10% To-Hit, Pathfinder

Special Units:
Berserkers (Fighter's Guild, Cost 90) More durable than in Caster of Magic. These continue being high damage
dealers and vulnerable to curses and ranged attacks.
Spellserkers (Fighter's Guild and Animist Guild, Cost 120): Now requiring only Fighter's Guild and Animist
Guild, these sturdy melee mage units are also the most easily accessible Caster 20 unit in the game.
Gladiators (Coliseum, Cost 175): These are the most durable units Barbarians can offer. They operate in a
similar fashion to stock unit shieldbearer with more advanced stats and hp.
Longship (fighter's guild + ship yard, Cost 140): Far superior to galley with reasonable building requisites and
cost. The only ship that comes with more than 1 figure and specializes in speed and melee (ranged attacks are
present with only 4 ammo). If Mariner Mastery is present, this ship can reach enemies in 1 turn. If enchanted
with flying, Longship turns into a general purpose upper-tier unit.
Gnoll:
Military-Oriented Gameplay
Characteristics: 60 growth, avg outpost growth, +2 attack, +1 move
Special Building: Altar of the Moon (required swamp)
Building Limitations: Monastery (+Cathedral/Temple), Maritime Guild, Armorer's Guild, Fantastic Stables,
University, +Bank, +Merchant's Guild, +Sage's Guild), Mechanician's Guild, (+Hanger, +Fortification), (+Wizard's
Guild, +Amplifying Tower, +Linking Towers)
Gnoll is designed to be an early rush aggressive race, even more so than Barbarians. This means terrible
economic potential on their own, but outstanding and mobile military units ideal for early war. A unique theme of
Gnolls is how some units appear to be a tier above what the unlocking building would otherwise provide. Players
starting with Gnolls cannot excel without early conquest.
Unlike Barbarians, Gnolls cannot build beyond the starter buildings and have merely average growth potential
(towns, outposts, settler production). Their armies, if unsuccessful at conquest early, will not be able to keep up
against more advanced, productive civilizations. Units are also unable to hit flying units effectively. Because of
these limitations, it did not seem fair to punish Gnolls with a poor armorer's guild unit, thus Jackal Riders
improved and moved to require War College instead (which can be rushed without Tree of Knowledge).
Additionally, as an early rush race, the magic market limitation was too harsh, thus had to be reevaluated. The
race is balanced by adding advanced building limitations instead.
Normal Units: +2 Melee, +1 Movement
Spearmen, Swordsmen, Halberdiers
Generic Mechanical Units: +2 Melee, +1 Movement
Trireme, Galleyrace unit cost Figures Melee throw/breath Range Ammo Armor Resist Health to hit Move Poison ToDefend

Gnoll Jackal Riders 190 8 7 4 7 4 0.3 4 0.3
Special Units:
Hunters (Replaces Bowmen, cost 40): Initially underwhelming, but with 3 modes of attack (melee, thrown,
range), ability to install trap, and a small 5% to hit bonus, it becomes formidable with experience, special magic
weapons, and attack buffs like 'fiery fury’
Wolf Riders (Stables, cost 70): Stables granting you access to a tier-2 like unit. Besides 5 move, it comes with
pathfinder to hunt for easy victims and be assisted by other mobile units and summons (e.g. hell hounds). 80
cost was evaluated as being too high for a rush race, thus reduced to 70.
Witch Doctors (shrine, magic market, cost 90): Shaman with mid-tier unit properties, such as high ranged
poison damage, double hp, and 2 charges of weakness spell. This is a viable unit for players who prefer to
develop the town economically first (see building requisites) and this unit's fullest potential is early in the game
when 'weakness' and poison work best.
Marauder (fighter's guild, cost 120): Updated beyond a first-strike shieldbearer with extraordinary stats. With
high base damage, they can defeat a unit without taking damage. Outside of melee, they are hard to defeat with
18 base hp and large shield, making them effective garrison units.
Jackal Riders (war college, cost 190): Mobile melee unit with 'cause fear' and top-tier qualities without the need
of Tree of Knowledge and thanks to being unlocked by War College, comes with additional stats. It does come
with several vulnerabilities due to its high figure count and low armor (e.g. immolation) as well as mediocre
resistance. Nevertheless, this is an outstanding unit for the low cost.
Halflings:
Economy-oriented Gameplay
Characteristics: 60 growth, +40 outpost growth, +1 research per pop, +2 food per pop, low unrest of conquered
towns
Special Building: Academy (required mountain/hill/volcano)
Building Limitations: Barracks (+Colosseum, +War College), Monument, (+Linking Towers), Armorer's Guild,
Temple, Hanger, Brewery, Hillfort, Warlord’s Hold, Witches’ Convent
Halfling are an economy race that needs spell support to assist in aggression. They can develop outposts into
towns faster than any other race, can build most economy buildings, and their population comes with food and
research bonuses, encouraging numerous well-developed gold, research and power centers and summon-
oriented gameplay. Note that animist guild can be built and modded accordingly to allow halfling farmers to
produce 8 food. Race can now even build roads, albeit slowly, with 'pioneer' unit.
Their troops are however mediocre to poor due to higher recruitment costs of early units combined with lack of
access to barracks and war college, requiring use of 'heroism' to be viable. In fact, a swordsman unit with
heroism + holy armor + discipline is borderline overpowered this early in the game, an option available to
players. All combat units revolve around 1hp per figure and are primarily ranged, making them highly vulnerable
to large shield and especially missile immune units.
For the late game, they needed something in terms of units and something not fully dependent on buffs. It was
decided a tactical flying unit with fairly low attack power fits the overall theme of the race best. As a balancing
factor, a few building restrictions that entirely impact battles (e.g. monument, linking towers) were introduced.
Normal Units: Lucky, higher unit cost, -1 Melee
Pioneers, Spearmen, Swordsmen, Bowmen, Disciples, Shamans, Magisters
Generic Mechanical Units: Lucky, -1 Melee

Special Units:
Scouts (stables, cost 90) – clearly not a combat unit, but you have access to a 'stealth' unit for exploration of
enemy territory and to keep in nodes near opponent cities.
Slingers (armory, cost 80) – improved somewhat with lower cost and higher mobility, and most importantly
becoming again a unit that can be recruited with armory. It remains surprisingly poor outside of life wizard
'heroism + discipline' strategies which fulfill unit's full potential to deal significant range damage while being able
to withstand a few attacks.
Rocs (Fantastic Stables, cost 280) – A flying 6 move first strike unit that can dodge arrows (missile immunity)
but suffers from lack of barracks and war college, resulting in mediocre stats unless buffed. Its main strength is
having the highest movement speed alongside Doom Bats for exploration, sneak attacks, combat stalling
strategies, and picking off ranged units.
High Elf:
Economy/Military Mix Gameplay
Characteristics: 30 growth, +20 outpost growth, +1/2 power per pop
Special Building: Tree of Life (required forest)
Building Limitations: Maritime Guild, Temple, Hanger, Brewery, Hillfort, Warlord’s Hold, Witches’ Convent
High Elves have economic potential due to access to all economy buildings, citizens that provide passive power
income, and outposts that develop faster than average They are now capable of building roads, albeit slowly.
Their downside is a very low city population growth rate and with smaller population, gold and production is
therefore lower as a result.
Their generic troops are good due to the racial bonuses. Mid tier stock units with these benefits become
formidable troops with heavy cavalry's first strike, combined with to hit bonus can result in killing an opponent
before they get the chance to strike back. They also have 3 top tier units with very different roles, for you to shift
around your strategies based on your opponents or lair targets.
The race design is not much different from Caster of Magic, but Pegasi were reevaluated and made into a proper
top-tier unit with high cost and maintenance, not a buff-dependent cavalry + bowmen that flies unit.
Normal Units: +10% To-Hit, Forester, +1 Resistance
Pioneers, Spearmen, Swordsmen, Disciples, Cavalry, Halberdiers, Shieldbearers, Heavy Cavalry.
Generic Mechanical Units: +10% To-Hit, Forester, +1 Resistance

Special Units:
Longbowmen (forester's guild, cost 50): significantly boosted, matching the relative power of the original Master
of Magic unit by having higher ranged, to hit, and even long range.
Druids (wizard's guild, cost 150): Magicians with priest-like properties that can also cast 'resist elements'. Their
racial bonus helps them deal high damage.
Rangers (armorer's guild, cost 200) : The most damaging bow-and-arrow unit in Arcanus, moved from Nomads
and given High Elf's excellent racial bonuses. The unit also has pathfinder, helpful to increase mobility of Elven
Lords, and stealth. The problem with this unit is how 'animate ammo', 'wall of darkness' or other counters can
render it useless.
Elven Lords (armorer's guild, cost 250): Damage and durability boosts, but with a significant cost increase. This
unit specializes in sheer melee force with first strike armor piercing and is a great candidate for buff spells.
Pegasus Riders (fantastic stables, cost 280): Higher stats across the board, particularly in regards to melee, but
at more than double the cost. This is a tactical unit that works best when Pegasus Riders can use all available
ammo. Pegasus Riders are however vulnerable to missile counters like 'animate ammo' and their melee
capabilities are comparable to a mid-tier unit.
High Men:
Tilted Towards Economy Gameplay
Characteristics: 60 growth, +10 outpost growth, Buildings cost 20% less, +1 rebel,
Special Building: Sancta Basilica (required desert)
Building Limitations: Fantastic Stable, Temple, Hanger, Brewery, Hillfort, Warlord’s Hold, Witches’ Convent
High men have average to strong economic potential due to access to all economy buildings and citizens that
can construct buildings at a 20% lower cost (including military buildings). Their downside is having an unrest
citizen for every city in addition to unrest modifiers.
This race had some controversial design choices. For starters, a -2 resistance penalty is far too severe to be fun.
The crusader unit in Caster of Magic was absurdly overpowered in the hands of a smart player to the point of
causing tedium. By reducing the resistance penalty, adjusting mid-tier units, and adding a more pure-might but
lower cost top unit, the race feels more three dimensional, varied, and ultimately fun. The race still specializes
quite well against defeating lairs and nodes with powerful high-figure units. The +2 figures theme has also been
expanded to more units, mainly support-type units.
Normal Units: +2 Figures to some stock units, -1 Resistance
Spearmen, Swordsmen, Bowmen, Engineer, Cavalry, Monks, Crossbowmen, Disciples, Magisters
Their troops start out weak with no bonuses other than a resistance penalty. However, the later stock units come
with +2 figures, increasing durability and damage output. High Men also offer a great variety of units, thus can
adapt to different battle needs.
Generic Mechanical Units: -15% Cost, -1 Resistance

Special Units:
Pikemen (Armory, 60 cost). These come at a lower cost in this mod, but with weaker defensive stats. These
carry the design of spearmen-like units being fragile (especially against ranged) but dealing high damage, in this
case 8 armor piercing hits at a base swordsmen attack level. Their high 8-figure count makes it an excellent
target for buff spells.
Squires (Fighter's Guild, 80 cost). Replacing Caster of Magic's overpowered 60 cost “Crusaders” with a more
damaging unit, with more armor but less resistance, and without healing spell at 80 cost. These still have large
shield, making them robust units against ranged attacks. Their high 8-figure count makes it an excellent target
for buff spells.
Knights (Fighter's Guild + Stable, 120 cost). Now follows the 'heavy cavalry template', but with boosts to
mobility, damage, and durability (large shield) benefits to being a racial unique. This is a very solid unit for
general use.
Inquisitors (Cathedral, 120 cost). Priest-like unit with a weak version of exorcise ability for melee and ranged
attacks, allowing it to banish lower resistance fantastic units if they fail a resistance check. This ability has a
stronger effect against raise undead units.
Crusaders (Armorer's Guild + Monastery, 170 cost). Crusaders have been redesigned as a top tier unit and with
different visuals. These are now 6 figure large shield troops with higher movement (3), good upper-tier melee
and durability stats, and can cast 'holy armor' on self or others.
Paladins (Armorer's Guild + Cathedral, 270 cost). Top Tier support unit (Holy Bonus) with decent but
unspectacular melee capabilities. Paladins can now cast bless spell (twice) and come with much higher
resistance, making them nearly immune to all curse-like attacks and spells and restoring some of the enjoyment
from the original where the paladin just couldn't be cursed. They also are immune to illusions.
Klackons:
Economy/Military Mix Gameplay
Characteristics: 110 growth, +20 outpost growth, +1 hammer per citizen, -4 rebels (if starter race), + rebels (if
not), bad race relations
Special Building: Undercity Hive Network
Building Limitations: Fantastic Stable, Coliseum, Monastery, (+Cathedral/temple), Merchant's Guild, Hanger,
Brewery, Hillfort, Warlord’s Hold, Witches’ Convent
Klackons enjoy the fastest city growth in the game. When combined with extra worker productivity and far lower
unrest (if starter race), they are able to surpass other races in getting cities fully developed, and earn excessive
amount of gold via taxes. Playing with retort 'alchemist' and converting gold to mana is a very powerful strategy.
The high production also can lead to producing a large number of military units, helpful when units (especially
later) are unimpressive on a power to cost ratio. Your military is defined as 'quantity over quality' and with
quantity comes accumulating upkeep costs.
It is preferable to rush settlers and cover as much land as possible with klackon cities to enjoy their low unrest,
and thus build your economy. You may raze enemy cities to allow room for additional klackon cities overrunning
each continent.
One problem with this concept in Caster of Magic is the sheer lack of unit diversity: pretty much just halberdiers
and stag beetles and they are rather boring units themselves. When the obvious strategy is to maximize the
number of klackon cities, it gets repetitive. There is more diversity in this mod, covering one of the main
weaknesses of the race in Caster of Magic and making it far more satisfying to play.
Normal Units: +2 Armor
Spearmen, Swordsmen, Engineer
Generic Mechanical Units: +2 Armor
Trireme, Galley, Fire Galley, Catapult, Ballistarace unit cost Figures Melee throw/breath Range Ammo Armor Resist Health to hit Move Poison ToDefend
Klackon Spearmen 15 8 2 4 3 1 0.3 2 0.3
Klackon Swordsmen 30 6 4 6 4 1 0.3 2 0.3

klackon Antlions 120 4 6 7 6 4 0.3 2 0.3
klackon Maiden Queen 240 5 5 7 9 2 0.3 3 0.3
Klackon Stag Beetle 240 1 17 8 6 8 22 0.3 4 0.4
Special Units:
Stingers (Armory, Cost 70): a halberdier unit with an added poison 1 attack per figure (6 poison).
Mantis (Fighter's Guild, Cost 100): 6-figure military troops that also has first strike and higher mobility. However,
with 5 base melee, the first strike is not overly impactful, but is yet another element that adds to the high
durability (e.g. 7 base armor) of this unit. The seemingly mediocre unit has been proven to win the game on
lower difficulties with warlord retort and unit buff strategies.
Antlion (Stables, Animist Guild, cost 120): A teleporting heavy cavalry type unit (lacking first strike) with lower
melee but 'merging' (teleporting) ability. This ability is restrained by a very low 2 movement, making it impossible
to use hit and run tactics . This is among the less cost-effective mid-tier units in the game, but a player has
opportunities to exploit the rare 'merging' ability (the only teleporting normal unit) with mobility spells, allowing hit
& run tactics.
Stag Beetle (Stables, Armorer's Guild, cost 240). As Caster of Magic described it, a true avatar of mediocrity. It
has been enhanced in this mod but with a 50% cost increase and a much more significant upkeep increase (the
upkeep cost of 1 in Caster of Magic was baffling and made race snowball in gold income). Base armor was
reduced to 6 but base to defend increased to 40%, thus has the potential to be very hardy with adamantium,
experience and holy bonus.
With Klackon's high production output, it is easy to generate a full stack of 8+ fairly easily and cover
replacements as needed. This is also Klackon's answer to flying units, being able to hit flyers.
Maiden Queen (Wizard's Guild, Animist Guild, cost 240). Later in the game, the mantis units (or Stag Beetle's
resistance) need a boost. This is a special support unit that grants +1 to all stats, heals, and also has caster skill
20. It is also relatively hard to kill, engages in melee, and even flies. Wizard's Guild is a hard to access building,
thus these will not come into play until the second half of your game.
Lizardmen:
Economy/Military Mix Gameplay
Characteristics: 70 growth, +30 outpost growth, NEW +1/4 max pop per tundra, cheaper, faster swimming
settlers (note, no longer with fewer rebel bonus)
Special Building: Baray (required river)
Building Limitations: Fantastic Stables, Ship Yard, (+Maritime Guild, +Merchant's Guild), Miner's Guild
(+Mechanician Guild, +Fortification, +Hanger), Cathedral, Brewery, Hillfort, Warlord’s Hold, Witches’ Convent
Lizardmen excel at early expansionism: marking your territory outside your main continents via fast, swimming
settlers. As an incentive to player, settlers are cheaper, more faster, swim, and their outposts grow much faster
than average. Early military is oriented towards expansionist playstyles thanks to favorable military logistics and
high hp units.
Race has limitations to gold and especially production buildings, slowing down construction and unit-recruitment
on an individual city basis. However, allowed enough time, Lizardmen cities are rather comprehensive in
economic bonuses and late military units excel at city defense.
More unit types were added, including a cavalry unit and a mage-like unit., and the design of an Armorer's Guild
unit costing only 100 (And acting like one) was challenged.
Normal Units: +1 Health, -1 Resistance, Swimming
Spearmen, Swordsmen, Bowmen, Shaman, Shieldbearer, Priests
Generic Mechanical Units: +1 Health, -1 Resistance

Lizardman Spearmen 15 8 2 2 2 2 0.3 2 0.3
Lizardman Bowmen 30 6 1 3 8 2 3 2 0.35 2 0.3
Lizardman Swordsmen 30 6 4 4 3 2 0.3 2 0.3

Special Units:
Carrack (forester’s guild and requires coast, cost 80) – Lizardmen's boat, helps with logistics.
Reptile Riders (stable + armory, cost 45) – a cavalry unit with lizardmen's hp racial bonus, and sacrificing a bit
of speed for armor. They are the only lizardman unit that cannot swim.
Mariners (armory, cost 65) – halberdiers with first strike. However, when fighting in the ocean, mariners gain
extra mobility and fire immunity (from submerging)
Javalineers (fighter's guild, cost 100) – now comes with higher movement and thrown ability. The race's buff -
friendly unit in terms of damage output, but fairly fragile for the cost and mediocre if no buffs are applied to unit.
Sea Hags (wizard's guild and requires coast, cost 120) – a mage-like unit with low caster points but 1 spell
charge of confusion. Their attacks is poison-based melee, a downgrade from a magister's ranged magic attacks
but appropriate for a race that does not specialize in magic.
Dragon Turtle (Armorer's Guild + stables, cost 240) was allowed to be a top-tier unit with proper movement,
cost and maintenance while keeping the feeling of being a tanky unit. Keep in mind Tree of Knowledge which
unlocks Armorer's Guild comes a bit later, thus unit needs to be able to do something besides taking hits and
stalling for time. With 40% to defend and the right tools, your dragon turtle can become a borderline unkillable
unit with some potential of reaching targets and damaging them.
Nomad:
Economy/Military Mix Gameplay
Characteristics: 70 growth, cheap settlers, road-like gold bonuses (without roads), NEW population cap trading
bonus removed, NEW +1/2 max pop per desert, NEW +1 Food per desert/tundra tile and +2 food per grassland
tile.
Special Building: Caravanserai (required desert)
Building Limitations: Granary, (+Farmer's Market, Animist's Guild), Fortification, Hanger, Brewery, Hillfort,
Warlord’s Hold, Witches’ Convent
Nomads suffer heavily from lack of food buildings, requiring a larger number of farmers to maintain army,
growing slower than 70 base growth implies (which is 10 less than in Caster of Magic), and reaching population
caps, an incentive for players to pick low-production territories or even disregard some locations altogether. One
added benefit to race is removal of a population cap trading bonus, which synergizes well with the original road-
independent trade bonus. Your typical nomad town will have 50% gold bonus as a minimum which is a
significant boost to your economy. While Nomads do not need roads for economy, their race can now hire road-
builder units, though these build very slowly.
Nomad units are highly resistant to curses and poison, and their typical combination of melee, thrown, and
arrows make them great targets for damage-oriented buffs and the effects of experience points. Chaos goes well
with this strategy with spells like fiery fury or blazing march, and if combined with life spells, units become near-
unstoppable when not facing missile immunities.
Normal Units: +3 Resistance, weak bow Attack with 4 Ammo
pioneers, spearmen, swordsmen, discipline, priests, magisters, shieldbearers
Generic Mechanical Units: +3 Resistance, +2 Ammo, +1 Overland Movement (Catapult & Ballista only)

Special Units:
Horsebowmen (stables + sawmill, cost 50) – redesigned to be essentially what it says it is: bowmen on a horse,
not a melee unit with bows, thus melee reduced in favor of more ammo
Kardakes (armory, cost 80) – their pikemen were given 4 bow attacks (please note armor piercing carries to all
attack types). This is among the most advanced units coming out of armory and kept as is by design as a special
racial unit.
Dervishes (stable + monastery, cost 100) – mounted monks unit that serves role as explorer unit and mobile
clergy support for nomad. This unit trade magic ranged attack for high mobility of light cavalry with pathfinding,
and arrow physical ranged attack.
Sipahis (stables + fighter's guild, cost 120) – With all 3 damage types and enjoying dependable traits like high
resistance, mobility and durability, this strong racial unique is a good target for buffs.
Cataphracts (stables + armorer's guild, cost 250) – across-the board improvement over sipahis and similar in
design as a mobile, durable unit with 3 attack types. A very good target for buffs, which tend to be a better
investment on high-cost units.
Griffin Riders (fantastic stables, cost 260) – similar in design (flying first strike unit), just with more armor, hp,
and to-hit at a higher cost. Its weakness is the average resistance score – an anomaly for the race – but having
an option for a flying melee unit for this race should come with a drawback.
Orcs:
Economy-oriented gameplay
Characteristics: 90 growth, -10 outpost growth
Special Building: Ludus Agoge (required desert)
Building Limitations: Cathedral, Hanger, Brewery, Hillfort, Warlord’s Hold, Witches’ Convent
The Caster of Magic design of Orcs remains in place. This is an economy-oriented race with cities growing
rapidly and access to all buildings, ultimately making orc population extremely productive while paying high
taxes. Additionally, all Orc units have lowered maintenance costs, so if you produce large armies for defense, for
lowering unrest, and for offense, you will save a significant amount of gold per turn. One could argue Orcs is the
top (or at least top 3) races in regards to gold income. Given that gold is expected to be plentiful, picking
'alchemist' retort can convert that into significant mana income and as an added bonus help your generic early
troops cause more damage in battle with magic weapons.
This is a solid beginner race, allowing access to most stock units without any racial modifiers, a couple of top-tier
units that are fairly easy to use, and practice with the empire building elements of the game.
Normal Units: lower gold upkeep
spearmen, swordsmen, bowmen, engineer, cavalry, disciples, shamans, shieldbearers, crossbowmen, heavy
cavalry.
Generic Mechanical Units: (no bonus nor penalty)

Special Units:
Hoplites (armory, cost 70) – a stronger than average armory unit, coming with a higher cost. This combines
elements of halberdiers and swordsmen to make a formidable 2-move melee unit. One weakness is the low
resistance but given the unspectacular nature of orc military units, hoplites look pretty good by comparison.
Legionaries (Armorer's Guild + Barracks, cost 240) – Caster of Magic horde was incompatible with Orc's
advanced technology and were redesigned to follow the roman theme started with hoplites, and now made into a
proper armorer's guild unit with high damage and defensive stats. Its signature characteristic is a rare 9-figure
count, therefore an excellent target for unit buff spells. The unit also has a few support abilities such as 'healer'.
It is a requirement to at least have veteran level experience and/or mithril weapons to make these competitive
against other top-tier units.
Wyvern Riders (fantastic stables, cost 280) – Wyverns come at near doubled the cost, but are given a total of
28hp, rare for a flying mobile unit, +20% to hit to increase potential of damage outside of poison, and very high
poison damage (14 with both figures). For best poison results, pick off low resistance units with this mobile flyer
or find ways to lower their resistance.
Beastmen:
Tilted towards economy gameplay
Characteristics: 70 growth, -5 outpost growth, +1/2 power per citizen
Special Building: Idol of Heavenly Bull (required desert)
Building Limitations: Maritime Guild, Cathedral, Hanger, Brewery, Hillfort, Warlord’s Hold, Witches’ Convent
Beastmen are the most traditional of the Myrran races. On the economy side of things, you can build nearly
everything and even have some passive power income through their population. On the military side, you have a
wide variety of stock and racial unique units covering various needs.
Normal Units: +1 Health, +1 Melee
spearmen, swordsmen, bowmen, engineer, monks, disciples, priests, magisters, halberdiers, crossbowmen,
shieldbearers
Generic Mechanical Units: +1 Health, +1 Melee

Special Units:
Centaurs (stables + fighter's guild, cost 100) – Versatile melee + ranged unit with high movement. First strike
and other slight boosts were added in the mod to balance the cost increase.
Chironean Guards (armorer's guild, stables, cost 260) – Essentially centaurs with far more impressive stats
across the board and nearly double the hp, but mediocre resistance.
Minotaur (armorer's guild, cost 270) – Reduced to hit but increased to defend (which benefits greatly from 'large
shield'). Stats adjusted accordingly but overall boosted to follow the mod's vision of top-tier units.
This is your option for extreme melee damage and buff potential to be hardy against ranged attacks.
Gugalanna (fantastic stables, cost 290) – Gorgon unit image from Master of Magic is back! This is a flying unit
with a -1 modifier stoning gaze (which has its uses against death units or with black prayer) and a high 50%
base to hit. Their resistance is higher than the other beastmen top tier units in case you need better protection
against curses.
Manticores were moved to Rakhshasa.
Dark Elf
Tilted Towards (late) Military Gameplay
Characteristics: 30 growth, +20 outpost growth, +1 power per citizen
Special Building: Tree of Magic (required forest)
Building Limitations: Maritime Guild, Cathedral, Hanger, Brewery, Hillfort, Warlord’s Hold, Witches’ Convent
Dark Elves have the original design - being the best race at using magic. This comes in the form of power
income bonuses via population and magic-oriented military units having ranged magic attacks, caster skill, magic
resistance, or advanced abilities. One downside to this is their fragility relative to other Myrran races and inability
to deal high physical damage. However, the top-tier units of Dark Elf, while difficult to obtain and mass-produce,
are among the most powerful in the game.
Emphasis on caster units gives synergy to 'astrologer' retort, allowing your stacks of caster units to avoid having
their spells countered by nodes.
The slow population growth dilutes the powerful magic income feature and also negatively impacts gold and
production output. However, the race can now hire units to build roads, albeit slowly, boosting gold economy.
The most significant changes to this race were additions to mounted mages (magic knight), eliminating the
overpowered library-required apprentices, and added emphasis on late-game military domination with
abnormally powerful units with high cost and building requisites.
Normal Units: Ranged magic attack, +2 Resistance, +1 Scouting range
Pioneers, Spearmen, swordsmen, cavalry, halberdier, shaman, priests
Generic Mechanical Units: Ranged magic attack, +2 Resistance

Special Units:
Adepts (Sage's Guild, cost 90) – Replaces disciples and acts mainly as a magister with caster 20 that costs less
and is more accessible.
Magic Knight (Fighter's Guild + Stables, cost 120) – The offensive stats may be mediocre for the cost (5 attack,
5 range w/ 4 ammo, caster 12), not much better than the cost 40 apprentices it replaces and less damaging than
an experienced halberdier. It is still considered among the best mid-tier units of the Warlord mod and will likely
be a staple unit for dark elf players.
Warlocks (Wizard's Guild, cost 180) – largely the same, but now a bit less fragile to magic and ranged attacks
(large shield)
Nightblades (Armorer's Guild, cost 270) – Unit is able to reliably hurt units unaffected by poison and is
surprisingly hardy with the added hp points. They also now have stealth and 3 movement.
Nightmares (Wizard's Guild + Fantastic Stables, cost 340) – A heavily redesigned unit, with weaker but
illusionary attacks, higher ammo, ability to cast 'terror', and modest boosts in durability. Its jack-of-all-trades
nature comes with weaknesses. For starters, all the bells and whistles pushed it to be the most expensive
normal unit in the game and also the unit with the most challenging building requisites. Its flying, mobile traits
help keep nightmares from trouble, but spells can easily defeat it. The 'terror' spell can only be cast once per
combat, diluting the relative power of an army of nightmares.
Dark Elf Catapult – loss all range attack and gains 4 charges of Fireball instead.
Draconians
Economy/Military Mix Gameplay
Characteristics: 60 growth, -10 outpost growth, flying settlers, +1/2 power per citizen
Special Building: Dragon Mound (required mountain/hill/volcano)
Building Limitations: Fantastic Stables, Temple, Fortification, Brewery, Hillfort, Warlord’s Hold, Witches’
Convent
The flying race in the game, Draconians can scout the map very fast, help settle territory outside your continent,
and are great for strategies that rely on combat-cast spells while the enemy can't engage them. They stay close
to the Caster of Magic design, with a few adjustments relative to newly introduced units.
Their units are excellent due to a combination of added stats, flying abilities, and access to an early 'holy bonus'
unit. Ranged units can benefit from being harder to reach with bowmen taking a similar role to Caster of Magic's
sprite unit when scouting lairs. Melee units are more convenient with flying with shieldbearers being a great unit
to mass-recruit due to lack of noticeable weaknesses.
Normal Units: +1 Armor, +1 Resistance, +Fire Breath, Flying, generally +1 Scouting range
Spearmen, Swordsmen, Bowmen, Halberdier, Shieldbearer, Monks, Disciples, Magisters
Generic Mechanical Units: +1 Resistance

Special Units:
Saints (Monastery + Cathedral, cost 140) – Saints have +1 stats to all (holy bonus) instead of just resistance
while enjoying other traits of priests such as 2 healing charges and decent armor. While this is designed as a
support unit, its ranged attacks are slightly stronger than ones from priests.
Air Ship (Maritime Guild, cost 200) – Air ship now loses wind-walking ability and not able to perform transporting
role but fully dedicated its roles as flying gunship/artillery piece instead.
Doom Drakes (Armorer's Guild, cost 280) – Doom drakes have been enhanced with more armor, hp, and +10%
to hit and as relatively better units relative to other top-tiers than how they've been in Caster of Magic (they were
overpriced and low in damage output).
Dwarves
Economy/Military Mix Gameplay
Characteristics: 20 growth, expensive settlers, +50% gold income, 2X resource bonus, +1 production per
worker
Special Building: Lava Smelter (required mountain/hill/volcano)
Building Limitations: Monument +Linking Towers), Stable, (+Fantastic Stable) Magic Market, (+Wizard's Guild)
Sage's Guild, (+Wizard's Guild, +Amplifying Tower, +Linking Towers, Hanger) Monument, Merchant's Guild,
Hillfort, Warlord’s Hold, Witches’ Convent
Dwarves are possibly the most overhauled race in Warlord mod. Economically speaking, their building limitations
have been shifted around with significant lack of magic-oriented buildings, making 'Alchemist' a retort worth
considering when playing race. Their gold and production potential is somewhat improved, if that was even
possible.
Military-wise, Dwarves have been improved. When consulted with other players, the general consensus was that
Dwarf was Myrran's worst race, having severe military deficiencies and gold building limitations that ironically left
them with weaker gold income than Beastmen and a few other races.
Therefore, Dwarves were given a set of mechanical units and troop-like units, mainly associated with top tier
buildings and very high magic resistance.
Normal Units: +1 Health, +2 Resistance, Mountaineer
Swordsmen, Crossbowmen
Generic Mechanical Units: +2 Resistance, +3 Armor, Mountaineer, +25% Cost
Trireme, Galley, Fire Galley, Warship, Catapult, Ballistarace unit cost Figures Melee throw/breath Range Ammo Armor Resist Health to hit Move Poison ToDefend
Dwarven Swordsmen 30 6 4 4 6 2 0.3 2 0.3
Dwarven Arquebusiers 65 6 2 5 3 4 3 5 3 0.3 2 0.3
Dwarven Hammerhands 90 6 5 4 8 4 0.3 3 0.3
Dwarven Crossbowmen 90 4 1 6 8 3 7 3 0.35 2 0.3
Dwarven Combat Engineers 100 4 1 6 8 3 8 2 0.3 2 0.3
Dwarven Steam Cannon 120 1 0.1 16 10 5 9 12 0.4 1 0.3

Dwarven Steam Tank 300 1 1 14 12 8 9 12 14 0.6 2 0.3
Special Units:
Arquebusiers (alchemist guild + armory, cost 65) – very unique troops, Their mobility and defensive stats are
quite poor, relying on cause fear and initial attack acting like first strike, but falling prey to ranged attacks. These
also come with weak ranged attacks. This is the kind of complex unit that is mediocre or excellent, based on how
you utilize it.
Hammerhands (Town hall + fighter's guild, cost 90) – demoted to a mid-tier unit with less melee stats (but flame
blade/fiery fury compensates for this weakness). Hammerhands do however move faster and break walls and
are far cheaper to produce. They could also work as engineer in building roads too when not as war.
Combat Engineer (University + Town Hall, cost 100) – now with triple the road construction speed and
redesigned as a support combat unit that has 1 charge of 'flame blade' spell instead of ‘disrupt’ that other
engineers have – this spell is excellent on low-damage but sturdy hammerhands. Combat Engineers also have a
moderately damaging portable mortar ranged attack and can build roads very quickly.
Musketeer (war college + university, cost 160) – carries a similar design to arquebusiers, but with much higher
stats. Their mobility and defensive stats (including resistance) are relatively poor and still relying on cause fear
and initial attack acting like first strike, but falling prey to ranged attacks. This is a very good target for buff
strategies and adamantium minerals and already get recruited with high experience (see building requisite).
Steam Cannon (University, cost 120) – Was considered a very disappointing unit, Steam cannon is given more
to hit to allow reasonable damage output. They still are nearly immobile and mainly used for defenses. Unit still
becomes useless if cast with 'web'
Huskarls (Armorer's Guild, cost 250) – Instead of top-tier hammerhands, we have a top tier swordsmen-like unit
that deals extreme pain thanks to armor piercing. It is also one of the most durable recruitable units in the game,
fitting the theme of dwarves.
Golem (Armorer's Guild + Mechanician Guild, cost 275) – It was promoted to a top-tier unit. Golem now has
added to hit bonus,higher hp and 40% to defend, and high mobility, acting like a heavy cavalry unit with decent
damage output. They come with innate resist elements, which benefits greatly from the added 'to defend'
Steam Tank (Armorer's Guild + Mechanician Guild, cost 300) – The ultimate dwarf unit, a ranged mechanical
unit that can also deal fire damage in melee (only when attacking). Its various defensive abilities and immunities
combined with extreme resistance points limit enemy options that could defeat the unit. However, with only 14hp,
these are destructible with the right spells and units.
Trolls:
Military-Oriented Race
Characteristics: 60 growth, -20 outpost growth, +1/4 max pop per tundra
Special Building: Frost Club Hall (required tundra)
Building limitations: Fantastic Stables, Maritime Guild, Monastery, (+Cathedral/Temple), University, +Bank,
+Merchant's Guild, +Sage's Guild, (+Wizard's Guild, +Amplifying Tower, +Linking Towers), Mechanician's Guild,
(+Hanger)
Trolls have been redesigned to be a purely military and very primitive race, so several new building limitations
have been established. Additionally, troll units have higher production costs and noticeably higher upkeep costs,
severely hurting your economy the larger armies you control.
Unlike Barbarians and Gnolls, Troll units remain impressive during the later stages of the game. Their military
characteristics are defined by regeneration, high damage, and very high hp ratings and have been enhanced
further.
Normal Units: +3 Melee, +1 Resistance, +200-300% Health, fewer Figures, Regeneration 1 or 2, approx +50%
Cost, +1 Gold Upkeep
Spearmen, Swordsmen, Shaman, Halberdier, Shieldbearer

expensive.
War Mammoth (Stables + Armorer's Guild, cost 290) – Similar unit design of extreme durability and high
damage but with much higher stats, costs, and 1 more movement
Chieftains (Armorer's Guild + Animist Guid, cost 290) – A Troll support unit that replaces magicians. It carries 2
spell charges of 'Raise Dead', which works only on normal units, making it ideal for keeping your war mammoth
units alive and reduce battle losses.
NEW RACE XuanYuan (Myrran)
Tilted Towards Economy Race
Characteristics: 70 growth, 0 outpost growth. +1 food per farmer. +25% maximum population, cheaper settler
Special Building: Military Workshop (required river)
Building limitations: Temple/Cathedral, Hanger, Brewery, Hillfort, Warlord’s Hold, Witches’ Convent
XuanYuan is a new race introduced by Warlord mod. Eastern Asian inspired with lore about civilization's origins
in Arcanus but cursed when seeking immortality and banished into myrror plane.
The race gameplay theme is strength in numbers (figures, higher population).
Economically, XuanYuan enjoys good population growth and late-game economy thanks to the maximum
population bonus and having all buildings accessible to them. The slight increase in food help feed the higher
population and larger number of military units.
XuanYuan introduces a varied unit roster with different strengths, helping player adapt to challenges. The units
come with higher # of figures. The increased figures (+2) benefit the 4-figure units such as crossbowmen and
cavalry units the most. A downside is their fragile nature – a 1 armor reduction with no durability bonuses other
than their higher figure counts.
Normal Units: +2 Figures, -1 Armor
Swordsmen, Bowmen, Cavalry, Engineer, Shaman, Shieldbearer, Crossbowmen, Heavy Cavalry
Generic Mechanical Units: -1 Armor, -15% Cost

Xuanyuan Dragon Horse 225 4 10 5 9 6 0.3 4 0.3
Xuanyuan Dragon Ship 300 5 9 6 8 6 6 9 8 0.3 3 0.3
Xuanyuan Immortal 320 3 8 2 10 8 0.4 3 0.4
Special Units:
Conscripts (cost 15) – Spearmen with armor piercing to compensate for not having room for +2 figures.
FireLancer (Armory, cost 65) – 8-figure melee unit with gunpowder, thus 'causing fear' like Dwarf musketeers.
Firelancers are strictly melee and excel at it for their low cost.
Alchemist (Alchemist Guild + Sage Guild, cost 60) – ranged unit with poison gunpowder, has caster points, and
a charge of 'rust'.
War Monk (Parthenon + Fighter's Guild, cost 120) – A superior monk variant with an extra charge of healing
spell, higher melee, durability, mobility. War monk does not have ranged attacks.
War Wagon (Stable + Mechanician Guild cost 100) – A 2-figure ballista with extra mobility
Elixir Alchemist (Alchemist Guild + Wizard's Guild, cost 180) – A caster 20 unit with a charge of 'endurance'
spell. Instead of magic ranged attacks, this unit uses ranged poison 2 gunpowder
AutoCrossbowmen (Armorer's Guild + University, cost 210) – A variant of crossbowmen with close range shots
('thrown') that can be followed with a ranged shot for maximum damage. The unit sacrifices armor piercing in
favor of higher base attack.
Dragon Guards (Armorer's Guild, cost 190) – A slow and extremely sturdy shieldbearer/swordsmen variant with
only 2 figures. These units are equipped with flame throwers, their primary source of damage, thus they should
not engage with fire immune units.
Dragon Horses (Fantastic Stable, cost 225) – A flying cavalry (mobile, first strike) unit with well-rounded stats.
Dragon Ship (Maritime Guild + Wizard's Guild, cost 300) – A 'ship' that attacks with multiple heads, not unlike a
hydra. The dragon ship has melee, breath, and elemental ranged attacks from its 5 heads, resulting in high
damage against lower-armored units. It comes with very high hp.
Immortals (Linking Towers + Armorer's Guild, cost 320) – An arrogant flying mage hero-like unit with caster 25,
a charge of regeneration, several immunities, and good life-draining melee damage output. The immortal
cultivator has high hp but is not armored, thus can be easily defeated by repeated low-damage attacks.
NEW RACE Rakhshasa (Myrran)
Tilted Towards Military Race
Characteristics: 50 growth, 0 outpost growth, +0.25max pop per forest. +1/2 power per population.
Special Building: Pool of Repentance (required forest)
Building limitations: Cathedral, Mechanician's Guild, Maritime Guild, Hanger, Brewery, Hillfort, Warlord’s Hold,
Witches’ Convent
Rakhshasa is a new race introduced by Warlord mod.
Feline race with a gameplay theme of fast bloodsucker carnivore units and multiple units (including a starter unit)
with stealth ability.
Their military moves fast in the battlefield, their lower-tier generic units are cheap to build, while their more
advanced racial uniques all come with the bloodsucker trait (if unit attack deals damage, 3 extra damage is
added while unit heals 3 points). This can include separate ranged attacks and thrown attacks, the latter allowing
a double-bloodsucker effect. However, a maximum of 1 trigger per attack regardless of # of figures.
Normal Units: +1 armor, +1 speed, -20% cost
Spearmen, Swordsmen, Monk
Generic Mechanical Units: +1 Armor, +1 Movement
Trireme, Galleyrace unit cost Figures Melee throw/breath Range Ammo Armor Resist Health to hit Move Poison ToDefend
Rakhshasa Spearmen 12 8 2 3 3 1 0.3 3 0.3
Rakhshasa Swordsmen 24 6 4 5 4 1 0.3 3 0.3
Rakhshasa Jungle Stalker 30 6 1 1 8 2 4 1 0.3 3 1 0.3
Rakhshasa Monks 40 4 2 3 4 4 6 1 0.3 3 0.3
Rakhshasa Wildhunter 65 6 5 4 4 2 0.3 3 0.3
Rakhshasa Sky Lantern 100 1 0.1 9 9 10 3 7 12 0.5 1 0.3
Rakhshasa Weretiger Mages 100 4 4 5 8 3 0.3 3 0.3
Rakhshasa Jaguar Warriors 120 6 5 6 6 2 0.3 4 0.3
Rakhshasa Blood Priests 120 4 3 4 4 5 8 2 0.3 3 0.3
Rakhshasa Rishi 180 4 4 6 6 5 8 3 0.3 3 0.3
Rakhshasa Ogre Lords 280 3 11 10 8 7 0.4 3 0.3

Special Units:
Jungle Stalker (Smithy+Mill, Cost 30) – a ranged unit that sacrifices physical damage with poison 1 per figure.
This unit has 'stealth' and can be recruited from turn 1, giving Rakhshasa a clear early advantage to lair hunting
over other races.
Wildhunter (Armory, cost 60) – This is essentially a halberdier unit with the racial trait bonuses. The unit cost is
higher due to the very useful blood sucker trait this early in the game. This unit is very vulnerable against
resistance-based spells.
Jaguar Warriors (Fighter's Guild, cost 110) – This is a shieldbearer with the racial trait bonuses, and
bloodsucker trait. A versatile tactical unit.
Blood Priests (Temple, cost 120) – The priest gains bloodsucker and racial traits without a unit cost increase.
For bloodsucker to work, damage needs to take place and blood priests have very low damage output, so the
ability is not as reliable. The ability can also be an opportunity cost to casting the healing spell associated with
priests, a guaranteed 5 heal that can apply to any unit.
Weretiger Mages (Smithy + Sage Guild, cost 100) – A sturdy caster 14 melee unit with bloodsucker and good
durability stats. Bloodsucker may not trigger if its mediocre damage output is blocked by good armor. Unit also
has stealth.
Rishi (Wizard's Guild + Temple, cost 180) – A sturdy caster 20 + psionic blast charge unit that comes with good
durability stats. The damage output (while lower than wizard guild units) is still usually sufficient to trigger the
bloodsucker trait. Another benefit of Rishi is illusion immunity, allowing you to see opponent invisible units.
Ogre Lord (Armorer's Guild + Coliseum, cost 280) – A powerful, sturdy melee unit with bloodsucker trait. While
the unit has impressive attack and armor ratings, the lower hp and resistance make this unit vulnerable in certain
situations (against 1-figure units, against spells)
Manticore (Fantastic Stable, cost 280) – The unit has been moved from Beastmen, given racial traits such as
bloodsucker in place of Beastmen's poison. Instead of ranged attacks, manticore has a weak thrown attack that
can help you trigger bloodsucker twice while attacking lower armored units or when thrown attack is buffed with
spells or adamantium.
NEW RACE Goblin (Myrran)
Military-Oriented Gameplay
Characteristics: 150 growth, 0 outpost growth, -50% tax income through tax avoidance, +3 rebels, bad race
relations.
Special Building: Mother Fungus (required swamp)
Building limitations: Armorer’s Guild, Animist’s Guild, Fantastic Stable, Maritime Guild, Oracle, Wizard’s Guild,
Monastery, (+Cathedral/Temple), Merchant’s Guild, Farmer’s Market, Fortification
Goblin is a new race introduced by Warlord mod.
Goblins are child-sized humanoid fungi, known for their cunning and cruelty. Most races see them as
troublesome pests rather than a race to engage with.
Goblin cities grow very fast but have very high Unrest, Tax avoidance (-50% tax income). Goblin army emphasis
on numerical advantages (consume less food, more figures, melee units could budding clones) but fragile and
die quite easily. Goblin lack of late game normal units and most of their late game offensive power coming from
mechanical units that both wacky and deadly to itself and others.
Normal Units: +2 Figures, -10% To-Defend, -20% Cost, -1 Food Upkeep, melee units could budding clones.
Spearmen, Swordsmen, Bowmen
Generic Mechanical Units: +2 Figures, -10% To-Defend, -20% Attack strength, -50% Health.
Trireme, Galley, Fire Galley, Catapult, Ballistarace unit cost Figures Melee throw/breath Range Ammo Armor Resist Health to hit Move Poison ToDefend
Goblin Spearmen 12 9 2 2 3 1 0.3 2 0.2
Goblin Swordsmen 24 8 4 4 4 1 0.3 2 0.2
Goblin Bowmen 24 8 1 3 8 2 4 1 0.3 2 0.2
Goblin Hobgoblins 40 8 5 4 4 2 0.35 2 0.2
Goblin Warbosses 120 3 7 5 7 5 0.3 3 0.2
Goblin Spider Riders 80 6 3 4 7 4 0.3 4 3 0.2
